As such, we\n   201→// need to mark the ancestors all the way to the enclosing relayout boundary in\n   202→// order to do a correct layout.\n   203→//\n   204→// Due to the high cost of layout, a lot of effort is done to avoid doing full\n   205→// layouts of nodes. See the comments on the layout booleans in\n   207→// LayoutObjectBitfields below about the different layouts.\n   208→//\n   209→// To save memory, especially for the common child class LayoutText,\n   210→// LayoutObject doesn't provide storage for children. In other words,\n   226→// it's the DOM node's responsibility to free its LayoutObject, this is why\n   227→// LayoutObjects are not and SHOULD NOT be RefCounted.\n   228→//\n   229→// LayoutObjects are created during the DOM attachment. This phase computes\n   230→// the style and create the LayoutObject associated with the Node (see\n   231→// Node::attachLayoutTree). Intrinsic sizes depend\n   250→// mostly on the content and a limited set of style properties (e.g. any\n   251→// font-related property for text, 'min-width'/'max-width',\n   252→// 'min-height'/'max-height').\n   253→//\n   254→// Those widths are used to determine the final layout logical width, which\n   255→// depends on the layout algorithm used and the available logical width.\n   256→//\n   257→// LayoutObject only has a getter for the widths (PreferredLogicalWidths).\n   258→// However the storage for them is in LayoutBox (see\n   259→// min_preferred_logical_width_ and max_preferred_logical_width_).
